0375869026|5.0|reposted from my blog: [...]<br /><br />A few weeks back, I ranted a bit (okay, a lot), about the absence of aspirational heroes in Middle-Grade fiction these days. For the most part, I'm still feeling tantram-y about the general state of things in this regard.<br /><br />HOWEVER--<br /><br />WONDER, by R.J. Palacio , goes a long way to correct this.<br /><br />Let's face it: there are books and then, there are BOOKS! And, by the latter category, I mean those rare gems that not only captivate us but also change us--for the better--by us having had the good fortune to have read them.<br /><br />WONDER is such a wonder. It tilted my obit, just a touch, and here's why:<br /><br />The story is about Auggie, a normal kid with a horrifying facial deformity. Yes, I said *deformity* although, like everyone else in the story, the impact of that word diminishes for the reader as we, too, get to know this remarkable little man.<br /><br />The story unfolds through the eyes of first, Auggie, then in sections devoted to the people who know and love him. It's a study in perspective---how each character views and copes with the daunting challenges of everyday life when you're always the center of unwanted, and sometimes hostile, attention.<br /><br />The writing is sublime perfection. Simple, and yet, so, so powerful. Palacio's voice carries the sophisticated eloquence needed to lift such a melancholy story into the realm of inspiration.<br /><br />One of my favorite passages:<br /><br />\\"Why do I have to be so ugly, Mommy?\\" I whispered.<br />\\"No, baby, you're not...\\"<br />\\"I know I am.\\"<br />She kissed me all over my face. She kissed my eyes that came down too far. She kissed my cheeks that looked punched in. She kissed my tortoise mouth. She said soft words that I know were meant to help me, but words can't change my face.\\"<br /><br />My heart aches, just typing that.<br /><br />There is so much wisdom in this book. I'm in no way surprised that so many have plucked pearls from its text. I am particularly fond of this one:<br /><br />\\"I think that there should be rule that everyone in the world should get a standing ovation at least once in their lives.\\"<br /><br />Wouldn't we all be better people if we gave more of those and received at least one?<br /><br />Read this book. You'll be grateful you did.

B001V5CIHQ|5.0|Rarely has an adaptation from a classic childhood story been so seamless, visually stunning, and truly entertaining. Originally written as a novel by J.M Barrie in 1904, and then for the London stage soon after, the legend of The Boy Who Never Grew Up entered American mainstream with the 1953 animated Disney version, which, although popular, failed to accurately capture the at times dark subject matter of the original storyline. Now, in 2003, under the guidance of director P.J. Hogan, Peter Pan has been given a live-action cast, the advances of modern filmmaking, and an overall look that is remarkably refreshing to a much wider age range of watchers.<br />Wendy Darling (Rachel Hurd-Wood) is a bright-eyed, and intelligent London girl who delights in telling captivating stories and sword fighting with her two younger brothers John and Michael (Harry Newell and Freddie Popplewell, respectively). But, one day, much to Wendy's dismay, her parents and aunt lay down an ultimatum: It has come time for her to grow up, and leave the nursery and her childhood behind. That night, after Mr. and Mrs. Darling leave for a party and the Darling children are all snug in their beds, a magical boy named Peter Pan enters through their open window and with the help of fairy dust and happy thoughts, whisks them away to Neverland, a magical paradise in which you never grow old, and all the characters from Wendy's stories come to life. From adventures with the pirates of the Jolly Roger, commanded by evil Captain Hook, to Indians and fairies, the delightful story comes to life once again on a grand scale.<br /><br />In the terms of performances, most of the young cast are first-time actors, virtual unknowns in the business until now. As Wendy, Rachel Hurd-Wood sparkles, and has an innocense and hidden strength of a heroine around her. As for Peter Pan, (this version is the first to use a boy in the role) the search for the right person spanned nearly three continents, and ended with the find of Jeremy Sumpter (known for his part in the thriller \\"Frailty\\"), who is without a doubt, perfect for the role. With his perfectly tousled hair and devilish good looks, he has a spark of confidence, charm, and a cocky little smile, (and still manages to convey his wish for a mother) that completely captures the character of Peter Pan. Jason Isaacs, who plays both Mr. Darling and Captain Hook (following the stage tradition) is delightful in his range of talent in both characters; Mr. Darling is an awkward, stuttering man who cares deeply and sacrifices much for his family, and Captain Hook is a seductive menace who terrorizes Neverland. In this version, the fairy Tinkerbell is played by French actress Ludivine Sagnier, who is at times annoying, but overall an interesting and amusing approach to the role.<br /><br />One of the things that truly stands out in this Peter Pan is the visual effects and the sets. The Darling household and London itself are beautifully done, and Neverland is beyond words. From the cotton-candy esque clouds above and the dense jungles with the hideout of Peter Pan and the Lost Boys, to the menacing ticking crocodile hunting Captain Hook, \\"Peter Pan\\" never ceases to amaze, as well as in the realms of costumes and makeup.<br /><br />Sprinkled with humor, and with a crackling script, a brilliant director, and extremely wise choices in casting, sets and costuming, and visual effects, \\"Peter Pan\\" is one of the best movies of the year and will continue to delight audiences for years to come.

0062255657|5.0|In this novella, a wise young girl lets the protagonist, a 7-year-old boy, in on a little secret:<br /><br />\\"Grown-ups don't look like grown-ups on the inside... Outside, they're big and thoughtless and they always know what they're doing. Inside, they look just like they always have. Like they did when they were your age. The truth is, there aren't any grown-ups.\\"<br /><br />As anyone familiar with Gaiman's work will know, he paints a spell-binding glow in all of his novels that can capture grown-ups just as easily as young adults.  Here, he proves that the girl, Lettie, was right: grown-ups can just as easily be pulled into the world he creates and inhabits just as easily as children.<br /><br />In short, this is the story of a man revisiting a mysterious and clouded occurrence from his childhood when a new lodger in his parents' house reveals the depths of \\"an ocean running beneath the universe, like the dark seawater that laps beneath the wooden boards of an old pier.\\"  Although he remembers little, deep down he knows the truth; of how the Hempstock women that live on the farm and the end of the lane saved him from a horrible fate and are keepers of a knowledge that has passed from many in the world.<br /><br />This is a nostalgic novel, told by an adult recounting the events of his childhood from a cloudy distance.  Although the fantastical elements of this book, like Gaiman's other stories, give it a distinct feel, Gaiman touches on themes that most adults can relate to: the emotional uncertainty of childhood, the feeling of a warm home, and the unsettling combination of fear and amazement that accompanies youth.  Once again, Gaiman assembles a modern myth that is impossible to put down.  I read the book in one sitting and was sad to see it end.  I recommend this book for any current Gaiman fan or any reader looking for an introduction to his adult work.  Although this is labeled an \\"adult\\" book, Gaiman's younger fans will likely enjoy it as well.

0062255657|5.0|Over the course of his career, author Neil Gaiman has delighted readers with his storytelling abilities. His almost childlike sensibilities have allowed him to reach audiences through various mediums, spanning from comic books to more traditional children and adult literature. With his latest adult novel, The Ocean at the End of the Lane, he explores a dark story with enough whimsy and emotion to attract readers of all tastes.<br /><br />The novel begins with a forty something year old man returning to the small English town where he grew up. His old home has long been demolished, but he is drawn instead to a dilapidated farmhouse at the end of the lane. When he arrives there, he begins to reflect on his childhood and the dark events that occurred at the place.<br /><br />He was only seven years old when it began. A quiet boy, more at home with his nose in a book than playing with other children, he was an outcast within his own family. We learn that the family is struggling with money. They decide to move him from his own room to bunk with his sister, leaving an empty bed to rent out. With the arrival of the renter, a mysterious opal miner, dark events begin to occur.<br /><br />The boy meets the three generations of Hempstock women who run the farm at the end of the lane. Lettie Hempstock, who claims to have been eleven years old for a very long time, immediately entrances the boy with her enchanting way with words and conviction that the pond that rests at the very end of the lane is actually an ocean. She agrees to allow him to tag along as she takes a trip to an odd place that lies somewhere between this world and the next. Upon their return from the strange place, an evil is released. Following the untimely death of the mysterious opal miner, this evil takes the form of a menacing nanny, who takes up residence at the boy's home. With the help of the Hempstock women, the boy must vanquish the evil while learning the true meaning of sacrifice.<br /><br />Neil Gaiman is known for his delightfully dark, whimsical fairytales. This novel is no exception. At its heart, this is a coming of age story that beautifully depicts the fun, confusion, magic, and sacrifice of growing up. Gaiman makes these sometimes difficult realities more accessible through his imaginative characters, situations, and pacing. The novel is completely engrossing, begging to be read in a single sitting. With an ending that is both poignant and satisfying, readers of all ages should definitely follow Gaiman to the end of the lane.iman is known for his delightfully dark, whimsical fairytales. B0084IG7KC|4.0|The Hunger Games was destined to be a blockbuster, from the moment the film began production. The novel, on which the film is based, was the kind of phenomenon of the level of Harry Potter and Twilight that would bring in a built in audience. But with the kind of fan devotion that the novel has, the movie also was tasked with meeting the high expectations of those who enjoyed the book.<br /><br />I'll admit, I was a bit hesitant to explore the whole Hunger Games craze. While I usually enjoy thrillers and adult literature, the novel had enough buzz to warrant my attention. I devoured the book in a day, and was convinced that there was definitely something to the story that I wouldn't mind seeing on film.<br /><br />The movie itself does an efficient, if not inspired, job of translating the novel to the screen. Jennifer Lawrence is the undeniable star as the strong willed Katniss. In the film, Katniss takes the place of her younger sister in the annual Hunger Games, a fight to the death between male and female tributes from each of the 12 districts of the dystopian world. Because of the limitations of the medium, we aren't given as much character development as the novel provided, but the actors do a fine job at trying to make each character fit into the world.<br /><br />In the novel, there was a subtle hint of political restlessness that gets mostly hidden by the big spectacle of the film. To be fair, there are a few moments where the filmmakers excel at providing deeper emotional insight, particularly during the death of one of the tributes. Unfortunately, the constraints of the film force the plot to move so quickly that most of these subtle moments get blown over.<br /><br />Overall, this a a perfectly fine adaptation of an above average novel. There were no egregious departures from the source material, so fans of the novels should be satisfied. Like the book, the ending is conclusive while still setting the foundation for the continuation of the story. If you haven't read the books or seen the movies, they are definitely worth the few hours they will take for you to experience them. Having experienced the novels and this first movie, I can understand the hype that surrounds the series, and look forward to seeing the adaptation of the second novel, Catching Fire, later this year.aven't read the books or seen the movies, they are definitely worth the few hours they will take for you to experience them. 0374533555|4.0|This book was written by Daniel Kahneman, who won the Nobel Prize in economics, despite being a psychologist.  This book is about how we make decisions quickly based on intuition, and only rarely use a more methodical approach to decision making.  According to the author, or more accurately according to a large body of evidence built largely by the author, we don't even realize how are decision making processes work and generally avoid having to think very hard.  This is not an assault on people's intelligence but merely a description of the way we work, as revealed by psychological studies.  Kahneman presents arguments and data that is hard to counter and I have become convinced by his central hypothesis that we are not as good at making decisions as we would like to believe.  This book is generally well written and the author usually introduces a new topic either with a puzzle that was useful in gathering data on a particular hypothesis or by relating an anecdote about how he came to study a topic and who he studied it with.  In fact, the only reason that I don't give this book 5 stars is that sometimes there are a bit too many anecdotes and it can almost seem like the author is the Forrest Gump of psychology because he seems to have been integral in every major discovery for the last 40 or so years.  Still, I really enjoyed this book and it was interesting to gain some insight into the ways that decision making processes occur.

He said, \\"Adults need fairy tales too.\\"  Perhaps I am misquoting him, thus is the slippery nature of memory that he explores in his new adult novel, _The Ocean at the End of the Lane_.<br /><br />I had no expectations for what this book would be about before I cracked the spine.  The fact that he had a new book out was enough for me to implicitly trust his imagination and skill in storytelling to but it sight unseen.  I was not disappointed.<br /><br />Wait, that is a lie.  It's over, and the novelty is gone.  I just finished it though, and I do have to say that this is one of the few books that I've read that I want to turn it over and start from page one again.  I it is thin, only about 180 pages, and Gaiman pulls you along so that those pages only feel like half  the length it actually is.<br /><br />What is the book about though?  It starts out as a relatively realistic novel.  A man returns to a childhood home for a funeral.  While there, he is inexplicably drawn to a house, and the pond at the house.  That's the first eighteen pages.  I thought it was going to be less of a fantasy story than some of his other books at this point, and even then I caught myself looking up from the page and exclaiming to no one in particular that Neil is a very good writer.<br /><br />The first eighteen pages of the unnamed man are just a frame to the story. I think she was a year younger though). No brief description I can give will do the work justice.<br /><br />What I can say is that Gaiman is a master at capturing a certain sort of childhood. There is a point where he is addressed by a nickname, but that is an evil being impersonating his father.)  Gaiman's kids are a mixture of joy and wonder cut deep with a heavy melancholy - I don't know about you, but I can relate to these solitary, bookish boys and girls.<br /><br />And ultimately, that's what makes Gaiman's writing so wonderful and accessible.  The characters are so fully realized, and developed and relatable that no matter what fabulous things happen to them, you are them.  This identification is helped in this book.  It is told in the first person, and the ego is string here.  There is noticeable amount of the first person singular, and the protagonist has some self-awareness, letting the narrative voice say that he saw himself as the most important thing in the universe.<br /><br />Overall, I have to give this book the highest praise. B00COQKE2M|5.0|Well, a little bit about me, to start. I'm 21 years old, I'm a senior in Petroleum Engineering at UT Austin and have played lead electric guitar for almost 10 years. I have grown up listening to Ronnie's music. Ever since 2007 when I first heard Dying Is Your Latest Fashion, I was hooked. His creative lyrics, his unique vocals (cleans and screams), and his overall \\"f*** any opposition\\" attitude have always inspired me to pursue my dreams in life without hesitation. Anyways, hearing of his departure from Escape The Fate and incarceration in 2008 was really quite saddening. One of the best had truly fallen. To hear of Falling In Reverse in 2009 was quite nice. Most of the music in the \\"scene\\" now just sucks, but Falling In Reverse is an exception. The Drug In Me Is You in 2011 really was a breath of fresh air, and in my opinion, truly rivaled Dying Is Your Latest Fashion.<br /><br />Fast-forwarding to 2013, this sophomore album by Falling In Reverse is no joke. They've changed their style slightly, while still remaining true to their roots... Personally, I say it's Ronnie's best work, but my congratulations doesn't stop with Ronnie. The entire band is incredible. Jacky is one of the best lead guitarists of this decade, Derek's riffs and breakdowns are absolutely brutal, Ryan's machine-gun drumming is almost unbelievable, and Ron's bass-work is quite amazing (especially in Born To Lead). The band still has retained a sense of identity when it comes to the post-hardcore/metalcore/pop punk style. Similar riffs, similar leads, similar breakdowns, similar vocals...<br /><br />Now to analyze the differences: Pick Up The Phone was the closest thing to rap on the previous album (the verse before the chorus or whatever), but this album takes that direction and runs with it. There are five songs with some rap on this album. Frankly, he's very talented at it, and I personally love it. I don't know many rappers that can tear it up like he can. I'm not really into rap, but this isgood. I can see it being an objective hit or miss though... I know haters will hate. It's just a matter of personal taste. Also, a couple songs on the previous album had electronica in them... This album, again, takes that direction and runs with it, as many songs have some electronic influence. Again, it's a matter of personal taste. I think the electronics are well-done. Then again, some will hate.<br /><br />All in all, I don't think it's a truly radical departure from their previous work. It's just their style taken to the next level... Those who paved the future are those who took a risk...and Falling In Reverse are paving the future.<br /><br />Here's a song-by-song analysis:<br /><br />Champion: 10/10 - This song is absolutely brutal. It's heavy as f***. It reminds me of Don't Mess With Ouija Boards from their previous record. The only difference is a 40-second rap bridge right before the breakdown. The rap is ridiculously fast, and it never fails to blow my mind. The lyrics are pretty cool too.<br /><br />Bad Girls Club: 5/10 - Haha, I gotta say, I'm more of a metalhead, so this song...ehhh, it just doesn't do it for me. Objectively, it's a good song and I guarantee you, it will be popular. Not my style, but I respect it for what it is. Don't take my 5/10 rating as truth, because it's just an opinion.<br /><br />Rolling Stone: 10/10 - Again, another absolutely brutal song. I love it. This has another small (really fast) rap part with some dubstep included in the breakdown. Being a fan of dubstep, this song never fails to blow me away.<br /><br />Fashionably Late: 10/10 - This sounds like The Drug In Me Is You, pt. 2... It's so good, it's a fantastic pop punk anthem of infidelity. Not that deep, lyrically, but nevertheless, it's a fun song :)<br /><br />Alone: 8/10 - Ehh, this song is what sparked all the crazy controversy... Frankly, I like it a lot. The rap is a little too much for me in this one, but whatever, because the breakdown won me over. It's a pretty badass song, and I feel like it's gonna pave a new future for this genre of music. His lyrics are a little...uhhh... Not my favorite. It's okay though. Great song :)<br /><br />Born To Lead: 20/10 - Best song on the album. It's heavy as f***. The lyrics are motivational and the overall performance of every band member is at a maximum. This song gives me chills. It inspires me so much, and if I ever make my dreams come true, I will cite this song as an influence.<br /><br />It's Over When It's Over: 10/10 - This song reminds me of Cellar Door from Dying Is Your Latest Fashion... It's got a little bit of rap and some electronica mixed in though. It's very well done. The lyrics, again, are badass. Very inspiring, and almost tragic.<br /><br />Game Over: 3/10 - I don't even want to talk about this song. Then again, you might like it... Don't take my opinion as absolute truth. I imagine this song will gain a cult following... Honestly, it isn't my cup of tea, though. It's not like it's a bad song. It's just... I don't even know :P<br /><br />Self-Destruct Personality: 10/10 - This song is badass. It's like Goodbye Graceful from their previous record. It was a sick rap portion in it as well, but it's concise and to the point. Love it!<br /><br />F*** The Rest: 9/10 - This sounds like Four Year Strong or A Day To Remember... It's so awesome... I like the lyrics a lot in this song too. The breakdown is my favorite part.<br /><br />Keep Holding On: 9/10 - A motivational power ballad... An anthem to the downtrodden... It's yet another lyrical epic. It inspires me to continue forward despite anyone or anything. This breakdown is epic as hell, too. Great song!<br /><br />Drifter: 7/10 - This is like a Hawaiian-country-punk song... It's kinda weird... I like it though. It's a continuation of the whole The Day I left The Womb/The Westerner story arc. You get a glimpse into Ronnie Radke's hardships in life.<br /><br />Where Have You Been: 10/10 - This song is heavy as f***...I love it. No rap. Nothing but amazingness. This honestly should have replaced Game Over on the record, but that's just me.<br /><br />Goddamn: 10/10 - This is so much like A Day To Remember. I love this song. I think it's a song a lot of us young people can relate to. I know I can. The guitar and riffs are amazing. Heavy, but no screaming. Great song! Should have replaced Bad Girls Club or Drifter, but again, that's just me.<br /><br />Rolling Stone Remix: 5/10 - It's fun. I don't really count this as a song though... It's just dubsteb and that's really it. I like it, but I just don't see the point of even putting this on the record.<br /><br />All in all, this record is a great summer release, and I know I'll be listening to it a lot in these upcoming weeks. Hate it, love it, who even cares? It's just a CD. For me, though, it's a little more than a CD. It's a story... It's a symbol... It's an idea... It's a message that says \\"Don't ever stop believing in yourself\\". This guy has been through a lot, and here he is today, doing what he loves... If he can do it, why can't I? Without enough willpower and motivation, anything in life is possible.

So now I will provide a five-star review instead.<br /><br />The band mentioned soon after the album's beginnings that they were nodding back to their glory days of the brooding, enigmatic sound that foreigners couldn't stop talking about. This excited me as [[ASIN:B003YM32GA Agaetis Byrjun]] and [[ASIN:B00006LLNU Sigur Rs]] are indeed my favorite records from the band. B00B7364H2|5.0|Classical audiophiles over a certain age will fondly remember Mercury Living Classics LPs. I am not part of that generation, but I vividly recall putting an old Mercury LP on the turntable (\\"recorded on 35MM magnetic film\\", the label boasted) back in the 1980s. I put my headphones on, and was blown away, thinking \\"What, this was recorded in the 1960s? How did they get it to sound this great?\\"<br /><br />\\"Simplicity is wisdom\\" is a succinct way to describe Mercury's approach to recording. Build top notch recording equipment, select the right microphones, find the best placement - and get out of the way while the performers do their thing. To an extent, this was also the approach used by RCA during their Living Stereo heyday. Mercury went RCA one better by hauling a customized truck with their recording equipment wherever they went - even to Moscow. But by the time Mercury had stopped making records, RCA had lost its way in the confusion of multi-miking, and it wasn't until the early digital era that Telarc resurrected Mercury's guiding principles. This is, along with its companion volume, the best sounding pre-digital boxed set you're going to hear, and some of these recordings still sound better than their digital descendants.<br /><br />For a smaller label working on a tight budget, Mercury built an admirable roster of artists including conductors Howard Hanson (also a composer), Antal Dorati, and Rafael Kubelik, organist Marcel Dupre, harpsichordist Rafael Puyana, and cellist Janos Starker. Many of the performers were attracted to Mercury by the opportunity to pick which repertoire to record, rather than having it assigned to them by A & R.<br /><br />Much of that repertoire leans toward the middle-brow. This is not the set for those who rely on Bruckner and Mahler for their daily sustenance. There are established masterwork staples, such as Beethoven's 5th, 6th, and 7th Symphonies, and Dvor&aacute;k's 7th, 8th and 9th Symphonies. There's also a lot of worthy off the beaten track music to be heard here including four complete ballet scores, works by American composers, and a generous helping of 20th Century music from Berg, Webern, and Schoenberg to Stravinsky and Bartok - and the world premiere recording of Corgliano's Piano Concerto.  Often, the program concepts showed an imagination seldom seen on the big labels: two discs entitled Music for Quiet Listening, military music, pops-concert fare, an album of Marches, and good old \\"sonic spectaculars\\" like Saint-Sans' \\"Organ\\" Symphony, and Respighi's Pines and Fountains of Rome.  There is relatively little solo instrumental music, aside from three discs of harpsichord music, an organ recital, and one disc of chamber music.<br /><br />I won't go into detail about these performances except to note that many show an inspiration seldom heard on the big labels. Although recorded under studio conditions, many sound like live performances caught on the fly.  In many ways, these are the kinds of performances we might have heard if advanced recording technology existed during the 78RPM era: not the most polished, but always compelling attention.<br /><br />Most of the discs are generously filled.  The exception is disc 54 which contains Dorati's first of three recordings of Stravinsky's Rite of Spring in monaural sound - the best of its kind I've ever heard. Some may quibble at the inclusion of this and several other mono recordings, but it's fitting since the Living Presence name was coined by a music critic who reviewed these early recordings.  As for the stereo recordings which make up the majority of the set, the sound is remarkably consistent: a strong center, with a discreet sense of separation at the left and right, immediate without sacrificing hall ambiance.  The dynamics are wide as Mercury engineers didn't alter the settings once an initial volume test was run.<br /><br />The set, which features the original LP front covers, comes with a generous and informative booklet. If the interest in this set matches that of volume one, it will sell like hotcakes - so snap it up while you can.interest in this set matches that of volume one, it will sell like hotcakes - so snap it up while you can.

B001D40U6Q|3.0|England, 1533. King Henry VIII is anxious to formally annul the marriage to his first wife, Catherine of Aragon, and to wed Anne Boleyn in her stead. However, the Pope remains adamantly opposed to both the union and the king's reforming of the Church in England. As a major schism looms, the king finds himself at odds with some of his most loyal friends and supporters, including Sir Thomas More.<br /><br />The second season of The Tudors covers what is generally considered to be the most pivotal period in the life of King Henry VIII, extending from his marriage to Anne Boleyn to the latter's fall from grace and execution just three years later. This period includes the separation of the Church of England from Rome, the martyrdom of Thomas More, the birth of the future great Queen of England Elizabeth I, and the rise to prominence of Jane Seymour, who is destined to become Henry's third wife. It's a rich period of history, dramatised many times (but arguably most famously in the play and film A Man For All Seasons, which focuses on More). The Tudors, due to its wider scope, has the ability and freedom to take this story and integrate it into a wider dramatisation of Henry VIII's entire reign, which has positive and negative consequences. Negatively, this is arguably the heart of Henry VIII's story and what comes after cannot help but be anticlimactic in comparison (though the producers of the show certainly give it a go). On the plus side the great time afforded the story by a television series means that the show can do some very interesting things, like devoting the entire final episode of the season to the hours leading up to Anne's execution, a move which succeeds splendidly and gives us what may be the best episode of the series.<br /><br />A noticeable gap in the cast is that of Sam Neill, whose character of Cardinal Wolsey died at the end of the first season. The less-well-known James Frain has to step up as his effective replacement, the ruthless reformer Thomas Cromwell, and does an excellent job. The show also brings in the legendary Peter O'Toole as Pope Paul III, mainly to show the reactions to Henry's policies in Rome. This is a bit of an odd move, as this storyline never really goes anywhere. The Pope commands King Francis I of France to invade England, an ominous development which is subsequently ignored, and is later shown having frustrated episodes over the work of Michelangelo in the Sistine Chapel. Amusing, but it forms a digression that might have been better spent in England fleshing out the existing, more prominent characters. O'Toole is, of course, brilliant, but his presence in this role does feel a little bit of a waste of a major casting coup.<br /><br />Natalie Dormer continues doing excellent work as Anne Boleyn, and has the difficult task of portraying the queen's descent into paranoia as she suffers miscarriages and earns the king's enmity. The show adopts a sympathetic approach to the queen, showing her to be distressed by her inability to bear the king a living son and innocent of the charges brought against her (though heavily indicating that she may have been promiscuous as a youth before meeting the king). Jeremy Northam also does good work as Sir Thomas More, the man of conscience and integrity who tries to balance his belief in his faith with his love for the king and dies for it.<br /><br />In the central role of Henry VIII, Jonathan Rhys Meyers shows early signs of improvement over his inert Season 1 performance. This may be attributable to his decision to 'do a Riker' and grow a beard between seasons. Unfortunately, the beard is rather unimpressive (a quarter-Riker at best) and his performance soon returns to a binary state of either being coldly inscrutable or insanely furious. Scenes which require him to smile or be jovial feel forced and unconvincing, and the less said about the spontaneous way he meets and immediately falls in love with Jane Seymour the better. The whole storyline withJane Seymour is rather badly handled, with the show deviating even further than it normally does from history (Jane had been at court for a year before Henry and Anne even married) and treating the relationship rather tritely, despite Anita Briem's best efforts with the material.<br /><br />On the plus side, Henry Cavill improves significantly this season as the king's best friend, Charles Brandon. He shows Brandon's growing maturity as he casts aside his philandering ways to concentrate on his family life, in contrast to Henry's constant flitting between mistresses, and also his growing spiritual crisis of faith at the things he has to do in the name of the Reformation. This is a theme that continues into the third season.<br /><br />Overall, the second season of The Tudors (***) is much as the first: it's tosh but watchable tosh which gets a lot of the details of the history wrong but does succeed in nailing the broader picture. However, the second season is elevated over the first by the richer, more dramatic events being depicted and some improvements in both writing and acting.Jane Seymour is rather badly handled, with the show deviating even further than it normally does from history (Jane had been at court for a year before Henry and Anne even married) and treating the relationship rather tritely, despite Anita Briem's best efforts with the material.<br /><br />On the plus side, Henry Cavill improves significantly this season as the king's best friend, Charles Brandon. B000RHKARY|5.0|The original version of this album on vinyl has been in my collection for many years, and has been a favorite of mine.  It contained twelve tracks, but this CD contains those plus the addition of another ten interesting bonus tracks, so it was worth getting.  I consider this collection one of John Mayall's four or five best recordings, considering the overall sound and song selections.  I got a kick out of Mayall's theme here of &#34;crusading for the blues&#34;; he is a fan and promoter of the music as well as one presenting his version of the music.  Many of the songs you will recognize and are associated with other artists, but do not expect that these will sound like those original versions.  Mayall brought his voice, arrangements, and the band's instrumentation to the sessions, and you will hear some different blues as a result.  Mick Taylor on lead guitar helps the sound to a great extent with his sustained guitar tone and swinging, tasteful runs.  The additions of Chris Mercer on tenor saxophone and Rip Kant on baritone sax also add to the mix.  The horns certainly give the overall sound some sophistication with a touch of R&B.  Also, I give credit to the Bluesbreakers for being able to play slow enough when required to carry the feeling.  All in all, this is a satisfying, fresh take on the blues that still has that sound many years removed from when it was originally released.

B00D8WJ9JK|5.0|A few years ago, I went to see one of my favorite artists in concert, Janelle Monae. I quickly realized though, that almost the entire crowd was there not for her or Wale--but the opening act, J. Cole. Within minutes, Cole had the entire audience on their feet and rapping along with him. I didn't know his music at all, but found myself moving along with the crowd and smiling just because the vibe was so good. I had to wait two years though before I could go and buy his first album though. I wasn't that impressed to be honest. I thought that I had somehow mis-remembered how good Cole was.<br /><br />Two years later though, J. Cole is back with the album I think he had always been trying to make. He even says as much on the brilliant \\"Let Nas Down.\\" It's clear the label and Jay-Z made him release a far different debut album than he had intended originally. This though--this is where you really see him.<br /><br />\\"Born Sinner\\" is both reverential as well as super modern musically. Cole hasn't hopped on the bandwagon of rap trends like having a girl sing all of his choruses or making the beats all dance tracks, but he is also not stuck in the past. His beats are clean yet with subtle touches that really elevate them like a jazz saxophone. He both samples as well as references tracks from the beginning of rap in a very respectful way-- A Tribe Called Quest, Biggie, and Outkast all make appearances. Also, Cole very smartly pairs himself with some great collaborators like the Dirty Projectors' Amber Coffman, Miguel and a choir who all provide a contrast to his rather deadpan delivery.<br /><br />Lyrically Cole is a beast. He is introspective and thoughtful, sometimes bragging, sometimes telling stories. He's not afraid to really be vulnerable and honest in his questioning of some of his choices and his daily struggles. \\"Runaway\\" was especially poignant as he discusses racial issues and ties that back in with his own family history.<br /><br />Now we do have to mention the elephant in the room though: Kanye West. It's not being unfair to compare the two--Cole is in fact begging for it. He knew exactly what he was doing when he released this album the same day as West dropped his. He forced himself into the conversation. And personally, I think his gamble worked. While ironically, Cole actually sounds like early West on a couple tracks, these two albums could  not be more different. Where Kanye's is aggressive and arrogant to the extreme (the \\"I am a god\\" track hello), Cole is human and self-deprecating (see title track \\"Born Sinner\\"). Kanye is off \\"making art\\" with minimal electronic beats, but Cole focused on making one of the best hip hop albums of the year. So yes, West might be more revolutionary and his hype machine is massive right now, but at the end of the day I'm going to be listening to Cole's album.<br /><br />Things that bother me: despite the fact that pretty much every rapper ever (including women) do this, the objectification of women on some songs does get annoying. The empowering message on \\"Crooked Smile\\" (featuring TLC) would mean a lot more if he could actually refer to women as neither a B***h nor a H*e.<br /><br />Hands down one of the best albums's of the year. I would recommend to every lover of rap out there. This album is personal and really pushes the boundaries of what old school rap artists might sound like if they were making music in 2013. It's not a throwback, but an evolution of rap music. It's modern rap in the very best way possible.<br /><br />***Update, Nas just dropped a remix to the already brilliant \\"Let Nas Down.\\" Seriously, go look it up. B0056BMK6K|4.0|This is a candid account of John Locke's rise to fame and fortune on the back of a cleverly crafted yet essentially trashy set of novels.<br /><br />What I like about this explanation of his success is the sense that he does not really care a damn about the writing itself. Forget the Great American Novel or even trying to be a successor to  Flaubert, Hemingway, Capote, Tolstoy or Zola - this is unashamedly pulp fiction and it is how he has persuaded us to buy this stuff that is the subject of this guide.<br /><br />Its full o useful tips but the bottom line is that you that you have to apply as much imagination to the selling of your work as you do in writing the stuff in the first place. This book, therefore, is as good a place to start as any other of the dozens of writers' guides currently on the market.

B004LGPBZI|5.0|The band has said that this album was inspired by The Beatles, Stones, Kinks, Hollies and Bee Gees. It is evident upon hearing it that they were not kidding. This is a trip right back to the swinging sixties. If you heard some of these tunes on the radio you would be excused for thinking you were listening to an oldies station.<br /><br />But it's not all sixties. There are several songs which sound current. One easily confused with Oasis might be `Standing On The Edge Of The Noise', which shares its name with one an Oasis concert video. `Kill For A Dream' is typical of mellow Oasis. And the guitars are let loose on `Four Letter Word', a slam bang rocker in the old Oasis vein. It starts the album with what may be a jab at Noel.<br /><br />\\"The battle is on and the song is the prize.\\"<br /><br />Let loose from the tight grip of their previous leader, this rock group drops the serious attitude and goes right for the gusto. Musically and lyrically it is catchy and cool, and like when your Mum's left the house and the toys and liquor are all yours, this record is all about fun.<br /><br />\\"Well here's my glass and here's one for you<br />'Cause these dark glasses need something to do\\"<br /><br />1963: The first single the band put out was `Bring The Light', and they might have done it as a reaction to Noel, who would never allow girl singers or the word \\"Baby\\" on an Oasis record. It took most people by surprise as it sounds so old fashion, like The Beatles doing Jerry Lee Lewis and his boogie woogie piano. Retro was not what people were expecting.<br /><br />1964: `Beatles And Stones' oddly enough sounds more like The Who than the bands it is named after. It is a pumping little romper that is very basic, all groove. It shows their ego will not be kept in check.<br /><br />1965: `For Anyone' is a beautiful jaunty jangly number done on folk guitars that could fit perfectly on \\"Beatles For Sale\\" or \\"Mr. Tambourine Man\\".  Not only does it sound right for the time, it is only two minutes long! `Wind Up Dream' with its harmonica is The Beatles once again, and it shows just how good these guys are at refining that classic sound into pristine, polished pop. U2 producer Steve Lillywhite did a fine job with the sound on this record. All the instruments are clear and the bass is always on an even keel, never overbearing. And Liam's singing is as good as ever.<br /><br />\\"Solid gold glints in your eye<br />A cheeky grin that really makes me smile\\"<br /><br />1966: `The Beat Goes On' reminds me more of the Kinks than Sonny And Cher. Melodic and flowing, it is a natural. These guys aren't punkers, they are the love generation. Its B side beauty, `In A Bubble With A Bullet' should have been put on this album as well. It is just a perfect pop song, sixties flower power all the way. `Three Ring Circus' sounds like a \\"Revolver\\" track the Beatles never knew they recorded. Just another perfect pop song on this record. Once again, this shows Noel knew what he was doing when he hired these two new guitarists.<br /><br />1967: The oddly named `Wigwam' might be the only psychedelic track on the album. It is for sure the longest. It seems to be about partying all night and then making up with the wife. It is an album highlight, though I prefer the dramatic guitar attack they use on the end when they play it live, compared to the fade out on the record. I guess the idea is to be up, up and away and with the repeating refrain of `coming up\\" it does work itself up into a glorified happy song.<br /><br />1968: `Millionaire' sounds like the Kinks doing \\"Beggars Banquet\\". This absolutely gorgeous tune is one of two songs about being driven in a car by someone else. We are dealing here with people who have a lot of money. They don't drive their own cars. They have someone do it for them. A far cry from the humble beginnings of Oasis when they did not have a car and had to travel by yellow submarine. What may be the bands most famous song, `The Roller', also sounds like it could have come out that year. The recording itself, production wise, sounds like it would have been right at home in the white album era. It was Gem's first Oasis song, written for \\"Heathen Chemistry\\" but for some reason it did not make it on that album. Noel described it as T Rex playing `Instant Karma', a fitting description.<br /><br />If the first song was a jab at Noel, then the last surely is a love song for him. Liam won't admit that but one thing for sure is that `Morning Son' is the most beautiful and deep song on the album. Its strumming folk guitar, slide guitar, tambourine and ocean waves make this tune seem like a daydream. `Morning Son' is timeless and a lovely end to a brilliant record, a record much better than I ever expected out of them. The beauty of that is I never expected another Oasis album, especially one with the band we have here. Who knew that Liam would be the one the others would stick with? We always thought he was the trouble maker. Now it looks like Noel was Napoleon.<br /><br />After Oasis broke up I had nothing to do with them. It was not until after I had a heart attack that summer that I found out that Beady Eye even existed. I grabbed their CD right away and it has been in my car ever since, easily my most played album of the last two years. With the exception of the last Duran album and \\"Different Gear, Still Speeding\\", if I had died, music wise I would have missed nothing. That is how good this album is. It was worth living for.<br /><br />\\"Thought that I died today<br />Walked off the stage<br />Faded away up through the clouds<br />To the gig in the sky<br />And when I arrived, the angels were singing this song<br />Yeah you know the one, are you singing along?\\"ds like it could have come out that year. The recording itself, production wise, sounds like it would have been right at home in the white album era. It was Gem's first Oasis song, written for \\"Heathen Chemistry\\" but for some reason it did not make it on that album. Noel described it as T Rex playing `Instant Karma', a fitting description.<br /><br />If the first song was a jab at Noel, then the last surely is a love song for him. It was worth living for.<br /><br />\\"Thought that I died today<br />Walked off the stage<br />Faded away up through the clouds<br />To the gig in the sky<br />And when I arrived, the angels were singing this song<br />Yeah you know the one, are you singing along?\\"
B005ERX1Z0|5.0|Good clean fun from start to finish. Joke after joke, great cars and a who's who of Hollywood royalty, ably assisted by &#34;him&#34; make this a comedy classic for every generation.
B00CELB94E|4.0|If you were expecting something that sounds like Oasis, or even \\"Different Gear, Still Speeding\\", your expectations may not be met. The band spread the word last year that the next Beady Eye record would be psychedelic, and nothing like the first album. Well they were half right. There are no psychedelics here to speak of. I was expecting `'Dig Out Your Soul\\" and I got something that matches the lovely Herb Alpert cover instead.<br /><br />Oasis Light and Other Delights.<br /><br />Let's give Columbia Records some credit for releasing an album with a semi-nude woman on the cover. Herb never had it so good. You may notice that some of the song styles seem to match the album cover and could easily be used in adverts to sell beauty products on TV. They are that happy, inoffensive and commercial. This is much more a pop album than a rock album. It is good, but it isn't \\"Different\\".<br /><br />The album starts out with the roar of `Flick of the Finger'.  Steady state chords and a frontal wave of horns come right at you. Hearing this and looking at the cover may remind you of Herb Alpert alright, Herb Alpert gone mad. The guitars are barley present, enveloped as they are in this wave of sound. Right when you are thinking this might be a great album a voice comes on reminding you that with the flick of a finger nuclear war could be upon us. I disagree of course, the aliens on and around this planet would never allow that. But I digress...<br /><br />`Soul Love' comes next and its soft delicate beat matches the album cover, but it is in total contrast to the album opener. This is not a Bowie copy, nor is it your typical romance song. It is more about mood, and the mood is pleasant. The song ends with a long quiet fade out which Gem calls an out of body experience. It would have been good for setting the mood.<br /><br />Except that they thunder back in with `Face The Crowd'. This song sounds unlike the rest. It is fast with a heavy handed beat but it does have a nice change in verse and a blasting but too short lead solo. Nice clapping section too. So we have heavy/light/heavy in the first 3 songs. It would have made more sense to keep the heavier songs together.<br /><br />`Second Bite of the Apple' would have fallen in nicely after `Soul Love' as it fits the vibe better after the latter's long outro. This was the first \\"Be\\" song I heard and at first listen this one threw me, it did not sound like their first record at all. It starts with bass and off beat drums, then percussion and what... vibraphone? Then Liam comes in raw, talking like he is right in front of you and wanting to know what Eve did with the fruit. This evolves into a backing with horns ganging up on a chorus. Then the entire thing repeats one more time before stopping instantly. Totally unlike anything Beady or Oasis has ever done and darn good.<br /><br />`Soon Come Tomorrow'. The bubble gum chewing bass player that I first saw standing on the stage during the \\"Giants\\" tour has shown a true melodic gift when it comes to writing pop songs. Andy wrote the more upbeat tracks found on this album, not something I would have expected after his \\"dream\\" songs. But his strong lead solo here is too short and not given enough time to develop. This tune also ends with a short fading musical section.<br /><br />`Iz Rite' is reminiscent of the energy and innocence of \\"Different Gear, Still Speeding\\". It sounds somewhat sixtyish and bouncy and with its layered chorus it is easy to see Justin Bieber and a convertible full of preteens singing along with it. It ends with jangly guitars but the music never seems to stand above the singing. Good song this one.<br /><br />`I'm Just Saying' is another fast Andy song. Liam calls it the Monkees sound. It has long stretches of singing with drum beat which get picked up by guitar runs. It hooks you with its beat and bop. Then it goes for the good times with its count by number backing vocals. This is a happy song that would have fit on theirfirst album.<br /><br />`Don't Brother Me'. When I first heard this I thought \\"don't bother me with this song again\\". I was getting bored with its simple lyric and style, and then I noticed it was only halfway over. It then drifted into a cool spacey vibe. Jeff Wootton established the bass line for this whch everyone worked around. Then he surprised everyone by saying he was not going to tour with the band anymore. It would have been nice if they could have done more with this part and less with the opening. This peaceful comedown might have been best used at the end of the album. The ending is pure minimalism, not shaken, not stirred, its Beady Eye chilled.<br /><br />Come back Jeff, all is forgiven!<br /><br />`Shine A Light' starts off with piano and strings, like a movie opening, its Andy's Scarface. Then it gets into a percussion grove and turns into a whole different sound. This is one of the most rocking songs on the album, but it still uses acoustic guitars to do it. This is not a Stones copy, more like U2's `Desire', which means it does nothing for me. But this album is a grower, so maybe I will grow to like it.<br /><br />`Ballroom Figured' is Gem's sweet little gem. A touching song played by one guitar. Liam's plaintive voice adds just the right feel to it. Originally it had piano, bass and drums, but during the mix they decided to stay with the single guitar. It does the job and sets a place at the table for our next song.<br /><br />`Start Anew' is a soft little acoustic song. Just a simple, short romantic number. It might remind one of `Married With Children', just a coda at the end of the album. But the whole album has been fading out up to this point anyway. So it is almost like the music is fading away. But electric guitars come in and add a little extra at the end. That's it for the standard album. Good job boys.<br /><br />Still the album has been coming down for some time and if you hear `Dreaming Of Some Space' right after this it really does seem like a coda sitting on the end. If you do not already know, this B side of `Apple' is part of `Anew' backwards. Dreamy, like the cover image, it too would have been a great ending.<br /><br />But the album keeps going with `The World's Not Set In Stone'. This song might have been the first of the new tunes, as it was played live a year ago. A soft tune, it relies on acoustic guitar and keyboard strings until the end, where it gets a sprinkling of piano and crazed sixties electric guitar.<br /><br />`Back After The Break' is one of the best songs from the \\"Be\\" collection. This one should have been on the standard album. Sure it is just a mellow tune but it has everything that Beady Eye does right. Nice melody, chord progression, singing thought and the recording sounds like it is coming from a radio lost in time.<br /><br />`Off At The Next Exit' might be the best song from \\"Be\\". It is just perfect, and sad, and beautiful, all at the same time. Once again everything is just right. Piano, soft drumming and soulful singing. This ends the deluxe album in a lovely way. If Beady Eye never makes another song, this one was a great one to go out on.<br /><br />There are 2 more new songs floating around Japan. `Girls In Uniform' seems like a total British tune. It skips along on drums outlined by guitar picking for 4 minutes, then a keyboard comes in to lighten the mood, which then stretches out another 2 minutes before it ends in simple piano notes.<br /><br />Then there is `Evil Eye', a nice melody built around guitar, drums and vocals. Strings come into the picture, followed by a guitar break that is not actually a solo, but more like accompaniment. It comes back at the end, where once again we fade away with piano notes. This too is one of their best songs. Another great piece that, as everyone says, should have been on the album!<br /><br />It would be interesting to know why the band chose some songs to be on the proper album and chose to leave others off. Most fansare already saying that the extra tracks are more than worthy. To me, all of them are better than `Crowd', `Shine' and `Brother'.<br /><br />It will also be interesting to see how the Oasis crowd takes to this album, because it is much slower and softer than the first Beady Eye album. Unlike the paid critics who spend more time complaining about Liam than listening to the songs themselves, the fans will find that once they get over the initial shock of how mellow the record is, the songs will reveal more depth than originally thought. And the more they listen to it the more they will like it. The band has given us an 11 track record, but they have given us 6 extra tracks. If you replace the original tracks with the extras that you prefer then you will have an 11 track album that is really good. This fact makes this album extremely hard for me to rate. I find it is not as good as \\"Different Gear, Still Speeding\\" but better than `Be Here Now\\". So is it a 4 or 5 star album?<br /><br />Beauty is in the eye of the beholder. If Amazon gave a 10 star rating my eyes see 8 stars.<br /><br />This is definitely their most mature album since \\"Standing On The Shoulder Of Giants\\".  But this is not a copy of what they have done before, here they are growing out and reaching up and they sound more original than ever before. This is the new sound of Beady Eye.<br /><br />I expect a proud Noel will be wearing a BE shirt under his jacket for quite some time. Secretly telling people, \\"That's my band mate, I handpicked them all.\\"eem like a coda sitting on the end. If you do not already know, this B side of `Apple' is part of `Anew' backwards. B00CU8OVIM|4.0|Born Sinner marks the return from one of the leaders of the new school in Hip Hop, J. Cole. His debut album Cole World: The Sideline Story was a solid album, however I felt fell very short to the standards his fans and hip hop lovers have been hyping him up to be, especially with the standards he set up for himself with his critically praised mixtapes The Warm Up and Friday Night Lights. 2 years later, J. Cole has come back with a vengeance more inspired and more confident than ever before. The album starts off incredibly strong with the opening track &#34;Villuminati&#34;, first showing how much he has progressed as a producer. The strings and Biggie sample makes this track one of my personal favorites.  The next track is a skit that transitions to the next song &#34;LAnd of Snakes&#34; that samples OutKast's most celebrated song (Da Art of Storytelling Pt.1) adding more percussions and beautiful female vocals in the background. This song has J. Cole venting about his rise to success and newfound fame. The first single &#34;Power Trip&#34; has J. Cole fantasizing about a girl he has been pursuing hoping he can finally get with her, a catchy song featuring a short but great contribution from R&B sensation Miguel.<br /><br />This album features 12 full songs with 2 skits and 2 interludes that act as 2 short songs. The first interlude being &#34;Mo Money Interlude&#34; which is not all that memorable, but the lyrics get the job done and the second being &#34;Aint That Some S***&#34; with Cole being cocky and confident. &#34;Trouble&#34; features a haunting choir singing trouble in the background. The lyrics encompass Cole's thoughts about the trials and tribulations that he experiences in life with women. &#34;Runaway&#34; follows the same themes about girl problems but in the perspective of other women, and in my opinion contains one of the stronger messages on the album that I'm sure a lot of people can relate to.  &#34;Rich Ni**az&#34; is a simplistic track about materialism but features J. Cole's rapping with more tenacity flowing faster than any other song on the album. &#34;Chaining Day&#34; has a very smooth soul sample riding throughout the song with Cole talking about his rise to success once again. &#34;Crooked Smile&#34; featuring the legendary TLC is my personal favorite song on the album. J. Cole raps about his physical insecurities and how imperfections make people better human beings. &#34;Born Sinner&#34; wraps up the album rather well with a theme of hope and nice vocals from James Fauntleroy on the hook accompanied with great instrumentals great lyrics from J. Cole.<br /><br />No matter how much I like this album, there are still a couple of songs that don't connect with me. &#34;She Knows&#34; was a hit or miss for me personally; I appreciate Cole experimenting a bit more using more eclectic samples, and I do like the production on this song as well, but the lyrics were insipid and the hook &#34;I'll be up so high, tryna get a piece of that apple pie&#34; made me cringe ... The song &#34;Forbidden Fruit&#34; was one of my most anticipated songs for the album and I was extremely disappointed with the end product. J. Cole and Kendrick Lamar together on one song should've been incredible, but instead we basically have a boring re-hash of A Tribe Called Quests &#34;Electric Relaxation&#34;. I feel like J. Cole added this song at the last minute just to grab the attention of Kendrick Lamar fans, and mainly because he added a line about releasing his album the same day as Kanye West which was only to Cole's knowledge less than 2 months ago...Kendrick Lamar was criminally underused and he even sounds bored on the song. &#34;Let Nas Down&#34; is an interesting track about Cole's experience from Nas's negative response to his radio song &#34;Work Out&#34; from his debut album and also serves as a tribute to his Hip Hop Heroes; personally I thought the idea of the track came off a little too corny for an album like this...J. Cole made himself sound like a whiny brat instead of vulnerable like this album was suppose to entail. I understand the sentiment of the song, but this song should've been a bonus track because it did not mesh well with the concept of the album.<br /><br />I must admit as well that the album has a very loose concept. I understand that J. Cole was trying to bring the dichotomy of his life to fruition within the album and trying to tie up the songs in a way where the concept would become clear to the listeners, but he didn't execute it the way I imagined. With that being said, Born Sinner is still a great album with a lot of great songs on it, and J. Cole is still a great lyricist and story teller. Support good Hip Hop and buy this album.<br /><br />Favorite 5<br />1) Villuminati<br />2) Rich Ni**az<br />3) LAnd of the Snakes<br />4) Trouble<br />5) Crooked Smile feat. TLCelf sound like a whiny brat instead of vulnerable like this album was suppose to entail. I understand the sentiment of the song, but this song should've been a bonus track because it did not mesh well with the concept of the album.  I must admit as well that the album has a very loose concept. I understand that J. Cole was trying to bring the dichotomy of his life to fruition within the album and trying to tie up the songs in a way where the concept would become clear to the listeners, but he didn't execute it the way I imagined. With that being said, Born Sinner is still a great album with a lot of great songs on it, and J. Cole is still a great lyricist and story teller. Support good Hip Hop and buy this album. B00CV5ZPA2|4.0|Kanye West is one of the most prolific Hip Hop artists to have ever existed. Each one of his solo efforts from The College Dropout - My Beautiful Dark Twisted Fantasy changed the hip hop climate, challenging himself to create cohesive albums that demand to be heard from beginning to end. Fans of Kanye already know that each one of Kanye's album had a distinct sound from College Dropout's soul sampling to 808s & Heartbreak minimal 808 drums and melodic singing, and even Graduation's synthesized instrumentals every one of Kanye's projects changed the boundaries of what Hip Hop could, should and would be. 2013, we have a new Kanye West album 3 years after the impeccable release of arguably Kanye's best album to date \\"My Beautiful Dark Twisted Fantasy\\". MBDTF was a musical tour de force, featuring maniacal instrumentals combining classical orchestration with hard rugged beats and unconventional samples of songs spanning multiple genres. It would be an incredible challenge for Kanye to succeed in creating an album that could at least match the ambition of MBDTF, as far as Hip Hop fans are concerned, his past 2 releases Watch The Throne with mentor Jay-Z and Cruel Summer with his label G.O.O.D. Music failed to live up to the levels of MBDTF. Now we have Kanye's 6th studio album \\"YEEZUS\\" and I'm sure music fans are curious to how this album will live up to Kanye's past classic discography. The title itself is enough to cause controversy, but just like the \\"no artwork\\" cover implies, the music should speak for itself.<br /><br />1. On Sight - Yeezus starts off with a banger of a song with the assistance of Daft Punk. The beat reminds me of Daft Punk during their \\"Homework\\" era, with their signature titillating synthesizers. Kanye goes on in familiar territory when rapping about himself. The beat will would do wonders in a club and it serves as a nice short intro to the album that sets the tone for the album. 8/10<br /><br />2. Black Skinhead - Premiering on Saturday Night Live a month ago, the sentiment of this song can match any punk rock song from the 90's. The lyrics are towards racism and the political standings of African Americans, but Kanye brings attention towards his place in society as a scrutinized black man. French house duo, Daft Punk, helped with the productions and I must say that the Marilyn Manson sample mixed with the loud, in your face tribal drums is an experience all in its own. The tone in Kanye's voice is angry and his screaming is infectious. 10/10<br /><br />3. I Am a God -  I wasn't a big fan of this song on first listen. The title of the song alone made me a bit skeptical to actually liking the record, but multiple listens later it grew on me. The song will be criticized as blasphemous and I believe that this record is the epitome of Kanye's ego, but I take the song in a different context. He never actually says he is God himself, he still humanizes himself to an extent by recognizing Jesus and the real God is above him. I personally believe that Kanye is representing himself as a Hip Hop God in this song, and it's hard to argue. This isn't any different than Jay-Z calling himself HOVA. It is hard to defend Kanye with him creating a song like this, especially with the elementary, uninspired, narcissistic lyrics.. but the musicality isn't half bad with more primal screaming from Ye. 7/10<br /><br />4. New Slaves (feat. Frank Ocean) - The first song released to the public since the album was announced through an ingenious marketing scheme involving public projections all across the world in various locations. This song features simple production, but the aggression of Kanye's ideals towards the industry is a breath of fresh air from his recent music. Although he takes the liberty to drop a couple of egotistic lines \\"see theres leaders and there's followers, but I'd rather be a d*** than a swallower\\" (it wouldn't be Kanye without it), he does however take the opportunity to rap about the government, racial andsocial classes and even his own position as a rap superstar. The Frank Ocean vocals at the end are nice and soulful which is really the polar opposite of the main song. 10/10<br /><br />5. Hold My Liquor (feat. Chief Keef & Justin Vernon) - This track has an interesting feel to it. The instrumentals have distorted and drowning effects which I'm sure is an intentional choice for the liquor metaphor this song is trying to incite. The story revolves around Kanye drinking his sorrows away and engaging in drunken activities. It's a cool track, nothing out of this world. Chief Keef's feature actually fit into the song and he didn't sound as bad as I imagined it to be. 7/10<br /><br />6. I'm In It (feat. Agent Sasco & Justin Vernon)- Braggadocios rap. Kanye using punchlines to describe sexuality. This song really reminded me of what Lil Wayne is doing right now which is not a good thing. I was entertained by some of the clever lines, but I found this song to be rather dry substantially. 7/10<br /><br />7. Blood on the Leaves - Reminiscent of his 808 & Heartbreak days. The \\"Strange Fruit\\" sample rendition of Nina Simone adds a disturbing ambiance to the song. The title of the track misdirected my attention into believing that this song would be about slavery. But instead Kanye takes a different direction and changes it into a song about women and his celebrity. I was highly disappointed with the direction he took this track. But musically this song is one of the most impressive on the album. 8/10<br /><br />8. Guilt Trip (feat. Kid Cudi) - One of my personal favorites on the album. Kanye and Kid Cudi collaborating on tracks together always comes out magical and this song is no different. I love the instrumental, despite the unorthodox use of samplings and weird undertone of the record. Kanye's singing once again, but this time in a weird filtered auto-tune. Theres nothing spectacular about the song lyrically, but production wise I love the record. 9/10<br /><br />9. Send It Up (feat. King L) - This is my least favorite track. Unnecessary and repetitive beat as well as a useless feature from Chicago's King L. This was just a boring mess of a song that really didn't go anywhere. Easily one of the worst songs Kanye has ever put on a album. 3/10<br /><br />10. Bound 2 (feat. Charlie Wilson) - recovering from the previous song, the album finishes off decently with the Bound 2. A song that really brings me back to the old Kanye with a sped up soulful samples. Kanye even sounds humorous again, which is a nice break from all the seriousness the album is forced upon the listeners. I liked the song, but ending the album with this song was just a head-scratcher for me. I really thought it would've been more appropriate to end the song with \\"I Am A God\\". Still I love the song and story which I'm sure was written for his Baby Mama Kim Kardashian. 9/10<br /><br />I'm sure all the backpacker rap fanatics will hate this album. And even some Kanye West fans would hate this album. But as for me, I always enjoy Kanye venturing into new territory he hasn't been before. Yeezus was really the most eclectic and most confusing piece of work Kanye has ever created, and I am honestly not sure if I can fully support this route that Kanye is taking with his music. But as a Kanye fan, I liked Yeezus for the most part. I just hope his next project would have a little more focus and better written songs.social classes and even his own position as a rap superstar. The Frank Ocean vocals at the end are nice and soulful which is really the polar opposite of the main song. 10/10<br /><br />5. Hold My Liquor (feat. Chief Keef & Justin Vernon) - This track has an interesting feel to it. The instrumentals have distorted and drowning effects which I'm sure is an intentional choice for the liquor metaphor this song is trying to incite. The story revolves around Kanye drinking his sorrows away and engaging in drunken activities. It's a cool track, nothing out of this world. Chief Keef's feature actually fit into the song and he didn't sound as bad as I imagined it to be. 7/10<br /><br />6. I'm In It (feat. Agent Sasco & Justin Vernon)- Braggadocios rap. Kanye using punchlines to describe sexuality. This song really reminded me of what Lil Wayne is doing right now which is not a good thing. I was entertained by some of the clever lines, but I found this song to be rather dry substantially. 7/10<br /><br />7. Blood on the Leaves - Reminiscent of his 808 & Heartbreak days. The \\"Strange Fruit\\" sample rendition of Nina Simone adds a disturbing ambiance to the song. The title of the track misdirected my attention into believing that this song would be about slavery. But instead Kanye takes a different direction and changes it into a song about women and his celebrity. I was highly disappointed with the direction he took this track. But musically this song is one of the most impressive on the album. 8/10<br /><br />8. Guilt Trip (feat. Kid Cudi) - One of my personal favorites on the album. Kanye and Kid Cudi collaborating on tracks together always comes out magical and this song is no different. I love the instrumental, despite the unorthodox use of samplings and weird undertone of the record. Kanye's singing once again, but this time in a weird filtered auto-tune. Theres nothing spectacular about the song lyrically, but production wise I love the record. 9/10<br /><br />9. Send ItUp (feat. King L) - This is my least favorite track. Unnecessary and repetitive beat as well as a useless feature from Chicago's King L. This was just a boring mess of a song that really didn't go anywhere. Easily one of the worst songs Kanye has ever put on a album. 3/10<br /><br />10. Bound 2 (feat. Charlie Wilson) - recovering from the previous song, the album finishes off decently with the Bound 2. A song that really brings me back to the old Kanye with a sped up soulful samples. Kanye even sounds humorous again, which is a nice break from all the seriousness the album is forced upon the listeners. I liked the song, but ending the album with this song was just a head-scratcher for me. I really thought it would've been more appropriate to end the song with \\"I Am A God\\". Still I love the song and story which I'm sure was written for his Baby Mama Kim Kardashian. 9/10<br /><br />I'm sure all the backpacker rap fanatics will hate this album. And even some Kanye West fans would hate this album. But as for me, I always enjoy Kanye venturing into new territory he hasn't been before. Yeezus was really the most eclectic and most confusing piece of work Kanye has ever created, and I am honestly not sure if I can fully support this route that Kanye is taking with his music. But as a Kanye fan, I liked Yeezus for the most part. I just hope his next project would have a little more focus and better written songs.

B00BNPWBOO|5.0|I'm one of the very few individuals on this planet, I suppose, that finds Primal Scream's 1994 effort Give Out But Don't Give Up a fairly enjoyable effort. Go listen again! You'll see! Yes, the neon Confedate flag on the cover was a little much (not to mention overtly obvious), and three of the twelve songs are downright unlistenable, but I dare anyone with more than one musical taste bud to deny the funky power of the title cut, or the Euro-boogie of opening track Jailbird. It was no Screamadelica, and I was disappointed, but now that almost 20 years and five albums have passed I now see GOBDGU as a pretty good effort from The `Scream. Or, perhaps, it's because the `Scream have released what I consider (and I'm a fan!) one of the most unintentionally hysterically funny and quite turgid `homage' albums in the history of recorded music with the bilious Riot City Blues. Woeful is a word that comes to mind. Ick!<br /><br />PS retreated after being crucified by not only the critics but also, and more importantly, by their fans, and came up with the dub-tastic Vanishing Point, the dark cousin to Screamadelica. In 2000 came XTRMNTR, an amazing album full of angst and electronics, and some of the best songs Primal Scream have ever written. Screamadelica remained my favorite, but this has rose fairly quickly and has been my #2 ever since. Evil Heat is underrated, paling (slightly) in comparison to the amazing XTRMNTR. As Pitchfork summed up: \\"so despite XTRMNTR's moments of glory, I filed it away and crossed my fingers awaiting its follow-up. After all, Primal Scream may be known for a lot of things, but consistency of style is not one of them.\\" Right.<br /><br />Then came the crap flood with the odorous Riot City Blues in 2006. The less said about this steaming, vomitous pile the better. It's interesting to note that usually quite reasonable allmusic gave it a 7 out of 10, and stated that it \\"is a much more relaxed effort, and benefits significantly from that stance.\\" Thealbum sucks. Take my word for it.<br /><br />2 years later and Primal Scream release Beautiful Future, which is marginally better than Riot City Blues. It is competent, holding pattern Primal Scream; no more, no less.<br /><br />I tell you all this to illustrate that even after all this time, and all these ups and downs (severe downs) you'd think I'd be done. The weird thing is, though, I find myself still getting excited over a new Primal Scream album, and this one in particular. It's not rational, I know, but I do. And you know what? This is more than merely 'good'. In my opinion it's not quite as good as Screamadelica but better than XTRMNTR. It's got it all, an encapsulation of everything good they've done up to this point: loved up dance grooves, 13th Floor Elevators style psychedelia, Stooges guitar crunch, spacey electronics...the one thing that surprised me on this recording that I didn't expect was the downright funky bass!<br /><br />All this would be window dressing if the songs weren't good. Not to worry, 'cause they are. Top shelf Scream, brothers and sisters, top shelf.
